The temple has only been built for forty years and needs to be repaired. There is a releasing pond outside the door, and the flowers and trees are beautiful. When Master Taixu came here, he recuperated here and almost couldn't get up. He was saddened by Shuanglin as a Buddhist example of Nirvana. Master Taixu deeply lamented the lack of talent in the Southeast Asian Buddhist community and cried bitterly, wanting to show Nirvana. This temple, although old, is solemn. When it was first built, it was raised by a female nun surnamed Chen, who had two sons and one daughter. The family was wealthy. They shaved their heads and became monks at Yishan in Fuzhou, and donated all their family wealth to buy a wooden boat and travel overseas to India. Her mother nun led them to tour the Buddhist sites in India. The older son's name was Shanhui. He often entered定samadhi for one or twenty days without eating. His younger brother's name was Xinghui. He entered定samadhi in Ceylon Island, the first time for three years and the second time for six years. He then left定samadhi. During定samadhi, he abstained from food and drink, and his clothes were completely ruined, but he was unharmed. When he came out of定samadhi, he was no different from ordinary people. The King of Ceylon was greatly shocked and led the people of the country to worship him and invited him to travel together. The Indians thought this was a beautiful story. But although Mr. Chen remained in定samadhi for three years, he had no wisdom or other talents when he left定samadhi. The whole family accompanied the mother back east and stopped in Singapore. A wealthy merchant, Liu Jinbang, believed in him and donated more than 200,000 to build this temple. The famous gentleman Qiu Shuyuan also donated 3,000 yuan. Later, his eldest son died, so the whole family returned to China, and the second son died in Hong Kong because he couldn't stand the cold. Now there is still a stone tablet in this temple, which is an extraordinary person after being rubbed for a long time. It turns out that entering定samadhi is equal to the hibernation of animals. Frogs hibernate for decades. If people use suggestion, put down all fate, and can last for a long time. I know this kind of psychology very well. However, now that bandits are everywhere, my original wish must be to eliminate world human war before I can devote myself to leaving the mortal world. I have a general understanding of the method of cultivation and I am definitely not superstitious, but now I have no time to do it. Lin from Yin County, Zhejiang, was my classmate and liked to sleep. He often lay on the couch after class and didn't get up all day on Sundays. All his knowledge was often researched and obtained in dreams, even during major exams. Therefore, when we stayed up all night, he said, "Why don't I stay up day and night?" Chili peppers are liked by Hunanese and Sichuanese. I, a Hunanese, am naturally among those who like to eat them. However, I am different from others. When eating, I must add garlic and ginger, and do not cook them. The mouth is full of aroma when entering the mouth, and I don't need to eat all day. If I don't eat them, my nose runs like I have a cold, which is very strange. Tang Bingnan, a famous gentleman from Zhaoling, likes to talk about Liao Zhai. He often said to people, "I have no other hobbies in my life, Liao Zhai, pig liver, and good wine." Then, he not only likes to talk about Liao Zhai, but also likes pig liver and good wine.

Second, for the sake of convenience, the newspaper can be entrusted to collect disaster relief funds. The money sent to the newspaper today will be published in the newspaper tomorrow. How quick and straightforward is this? If a certain amount is collected, the newspaper will be entrusted to remit it. The remaining odd amounts will still be stored there and remitted to the disaster area after a certain amount has been accumulated. However, disaster relief is always very urgent and often a drop in the bucket or water far from the fire and too slow to help. If the gentry and merchants in Shanghai come out to promote it, the actors will not be enthusiastic. However, that trick has been played several times, and there is not much left after a day's expenses. There is also no point in doing this often, so you want to create some new tricks to stir up the moment and raise tens of thousands of dollars.

Local News

Ministry of Finance Actively Promoting the Abolition of Likin 140

The Likin Abolition Committee is responsible for preparing the implementation in various provinces. Before the implementation in various provinces, new legitimate taxes will be established. Since the Ministry of Finance of the National Government appointed Mr. Li Jihong, a counselor of the Ministry, to Shanghai to set up an office for the Likin Abolition Committee, he has been making every effort to contact the personnel in charge of likin in various provinces to carry out the abolition of likin. Yesterday, a reporter from the Zhendan News Agency visited an important official at the office to inquire about the recent progress of the committee. The details are as follows: Since the establishment of the Likin Abolition Committee in various provinces, telegrams have been sent to the finance departments of various provinces to send personnel in charge to Shanghai for consultation with the committee. The main objectives are twofold: (A) to hold the personnel in charge in various provinces responsible for the implementation of the abolition of likin; (B) to instruct the committee to provide guidance and find solutions when provinces encounter special difficulties. Currently, personnel in charge from Liaoning, Hubei, Hunan, Shandong, Jiangxi, Jiangsu, Guangdong, and four provinces of Yunnan, Sichuan, Guizhou, and Fujian have reported. The committee has contacted the provinces through official documents. Except for Jiangxi and Jiangsu provinces, where likin is directly managed by the central government, the remaining provinces share the same difficulty in finding methods to compensate for the abolition of likin. Therefore, the representatives of the provinces have held one meeting, but there have been no other formal meetings. Ministry of Finance Survey: In order to investigate the likin situation in various provinces and methods of compensation, the Ministry of Finance has formulated a projection table and distributed it to various provinces to fill out and submit to the committee. The content of the table includes: (1) the total amount of likin abolished nationwide; (2) the special taxes to be levied in accordance with the situation in each province; (3) the estimated revenue of special taxes; (4) the types of important products in each province. Implementation Time: It is heard that the implementation of likin abolition will take place on the Double Tenth Festival, and the committee is supervising the preparation for implementation in various provinces. Furthermore, it is imperative that new compensatory taxes be completed by the Double Tenth Festival. It is heard that the resolution of the Likin Abolition Committee is being handled, and it is specially recorded as follows: Likin Abolition Plan: Outline for Abolishing Domestic Transit Taxes, Reforming Special Consumption Taxes. Based on the resolutions of the National Financial Conference and the Likin Abolition Circular, the Ministry of Finance abolishes all domestic likin and similar transit taxes nationwide, and simultaneously implements special consumption taxes as compensation, and formulates the following implementation outline: (A) Steps to Abolish Domestic Transit Taxes: First, the following items shall be abolished by the provinces on a scheduled basis. By the end of September, bureaus and cards shall be abolished or merged separately. By the end of November at the latest, all types of bureaus and cards shall be abolished: (1) Likin; (2) various commodity taxes reformed from likin; (3) various inland taxes and levies containing the nature of transit taxes; (4) Landed tax. Second, the following items shall be abolished by the Ministry of Finance on a scheduled basis: items 1, 2, and 3 shall be abolished by the end of November; items 4, 5, 6, and 7 shall be abolished by the end of December: (1) Railway freight tax; (2) Parcel post likin; (3) Customs stations and surtaxes 50 miles outside the commercial ports; (4) Import duties and surtaxes of the Maritime and Land New Customs; (5) Re-import duties and surtaxes of the Maritime and Land New Customs; (6) Duties and surtaxes of the Maritime and Land New Customs from this port to that port; (7) Customs duties and surtaxes within 50 miles of the commercial ports. Customs stations on land borders and coastal customs collecting national border import and export taxes are not subject to abolition. (B) Principles for Reforming Special Consumption Taxes: First, for domestic goods: (1) The tax amount of special consumption taxes reformed by abolishing likin shall not be higher than the original tax amount, but luxury goods are not subject to this restriction; (2) When reforming special consumption taxes, efforts shall be made to avoid setting up checkpoints at every stage, and there shall be no repeated levies or obstructions; (3) The fiscal authorities must first consult the opinions of commercial groups on the collection methods of special consumption taxes; (4) In the event of items that must be encouraged or protected, the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce shall jointly formulate encouragement or protection measures with representatives of commercial groups; (5) Daily necessities for people's livelihood, such as rice, wheat, native cloth, firewood, and charcoal, must be tax-free; (6) Fertilizers used in agriculture must be tax-free; (7) Various machines used in agriculture must be tax-free; (8) The items listed in this outline for taxation and manufactured goods must be tax-free; (9) Educational supplies and items that promote culture must be tax-free; (10) Small-scale items with small production must be tax-free. Second, for foreign goods: (1) Before tariff autonomy, in the event of items that are the same as domestically taxed goods, consumption taxes shall still be levied in addition to the import duties of the Maritime and Land New Customs, in accordance with Japanese precedents; (2) After tariff autonomy, the system of one tax per item shall be followed, and no further taxes shall be levied after one tax is paid, or the previous method shall still be followed, as determined at the time. (C) Types of Special Consumption Taxes Reformed: First, the Ministry of Finance shall levy three types of consumption taxes: (1) Grain tax; (2) Textile tax; (3) Factory tax. The flour tax will be levied first, followed by the silk, ramie, and cotton yarn taxes. When the above three types are levied, the Ministry of Finance shall notify the Ministry of Finance to negotiate and divide the collection. The original taxes collected by the Ministry of Finance within the scope of likin shall be verified and the Ministry of Finance shall propose one of the three types in accordance with the amount. Before the Ministry of Finance levies the tax, it may entrust the provincial finance department to collect it on its behalf. For those who have already paid the factory tax on silk, ramie, and cotton yarn, the tax bill may be used to offset the textile tax when it is paid. Second, the Ministry of Finance shall temporarily entrust the provincial finance departments to levy several types of special consumption taxes from the following: (1) Oils; (2) Teas; (3) Paper; (4) Tin foil; (5) Seafood; (6) Wood; (7) Ceramics; (8) Livestock (excluding livestock used for farming and domestic animals); (9) Medicinal materials; (10) Lacquer; (11) Bulk mineral products (only leather, fur, and feathers); (12) Bulk mineral products (tax shall only be levied on mines); (13) Cocoons (cocoon tax shall be refunded when silk tax is collected); (14) Silk (silk tax shall be refunded when silk fabric tax is collected); (15) Soybeans (soybean tax shall be refunded when oil tax is collected); (16) Cotton (cotton tax shall be refunded when yarn tax is collected). The amount of consumption tax to be levied on the above items shall be selected and reported to the Ministry for approval by the provincial finance departments in accordance with local conditions. The principle is as follows: (1) Tax shall only be levied on the place of origin for the above items, and after one tax is paid, it shall be valid throughout the country, and no other levies shall be collected; (2) Tax shall not be levied on items that are not produced in bulk within the province; (3) The provincial finance departments shall be responsible for the special consumption taxes levied by the provinces, and bureaus shall be set up to handle goods of the same nature jointly in order to save expenses.

Petition for Exemption from Tax on Writing Brushes and Ink 142

The Writing Brush and Ink Trade Association submitted a document to the Chamber of Commerce, stating that ink is an educational supply and should be exempted from tax in accordance with the example of books, in order to promote education and alleviate the difficulties of Jiangsu merchants, requesting that it be forwarded to the government. An investigation reveals that writing brushes and ink are educational supplies and are a national treasure of thousands of years. Historical records show that they were highly regarded. In the past, goods were transported without tax in every dynasty. During the Tongzhi and Guangxu periods of the Qing Dynasty, candidates only needed to mark the location of the examination hall or the provincial examination when rushing to take the examination. Upon passing through checkpoints, they were immediately verified and released without any obstruction or demands for payment. After the abolition of the imperial examination system, European customs gradually spread to the East, and talents in the country eagerly sought Western learning. As a result, high-quality writing brushes and ink were not sold well, and only medium and low-quality goods were sold. The business position of those in the industry has also changed as a result. The focus of the industry has shifted to coastal commercial ports. Goods must pass through customs, and the customs officials are mostly Westerners who are unfamiliar with Chinese history. They temporarily estimate the value of writing brushes and ink for taxation. At that time, writing brush and ink merchants lacked unity and a joint voice. The practice has continued for more than 20 years, and the accumulated habits have become increasingly serious. Whether it is customs, likin stations, or postal parcels, taxes are levied in all cases. In addition, the cost of living is rising and wages are increasing, which has endlessly increased costs. If merchants want to transport goods, their capital is not guaranteed. If they want to close their businesses, their families will starve. The national treasure of China has declined to such an extent, and who knows that the shops are filled with various steel pens, pencils, fountain pens, Japanese writing brushes, ink, and natural ink? Foreign imports are flourishing. An investigation reveals that the raw materials for writing brushes and ink, such as goat hair and brush tubes, come from Zhejiang, weasel and rabbit skins come from the Northwest, and Guang glue and borneol come from Guangdong. Ink soot and musk come from Sichuan, Guizhou, Guangxi, and Yunnan. Twenty years ago, Huizhou merchants set up soot houses in the mountains of those provinces to buy tung oil for lighting and collecting soot, as well as musk and rabbit hair. Later, American merchants monopolized the lighting and soot production, and the capital was not guaranteed. They had to switch to imported Western soot. They paid consolidated taxes and likin in the interior, and import and export taxes at customs. The repeated levies exceeded 20%. An investigation reveals that the manufacturing process relies entirely on manual labor. Taking Shanghai as an example, even in this time of decline, there are still more than 3,000 workers. Wages have increased by 50% since 1927, and other benefits have also increased accordingly, but the selling price is not as good as before. Huizhou ink is sold for only 44 taels of silver per 100 catties, which is about 40% less than 10 years ago. Writing brushes have also been affected and are sold in the 21 provinces of Jilin, Heilongjiang, Hebei, Shandong, Shanxi, Shaanxi, Gansu, Henan, Sichuan, Guangxi, Guangdong, Fujian, Guizhou, Yunnan, Anhui, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and overseas, with annual sales of about 300,000 yuan. The overseas sales are to Japan, Korea, Taiwan, Saigon, the South Seas Islands, San Francisco, and other places, with annual sales of about 50,000 yuan. The annual sales of the Shanghai stores are about 150,000 yuan. The total annual sales of Shanghai are about 500,000 yuan. In addition to sea transportation, most of the goods are transported by postal parcels. The estimated cost of ink is 80 taels of silver per 100 catties, and the Huizhou tax is 4 taels. The tax rate is 1/11 of the selling price. The estimated cost of each 100 writing brushes is 2-3 yuan in foreign currency, but now that foreign currency has been converted to silver, the estimated cost is 5-6 taels of silver, which is even higher than 1/11 of the wholesale price. Furthermore, the raw materials for writing brushes and ink have already been subject to repeated taxation and likin at customs and checkpoints. Moreover, the manufactured educational supplies, writing brushes and ink, are used to promote learning for students, yet they are subject to a tax rate of 1/11. This is rare in civilized countries. The writing brush and ink merchants are suffering and will inevitably go bankrupt. As a result, the youth of the country will lose their means of learning. Thinking of this, we cannot help but hate the writing brush and ink merchants of the past who did not seek self-improvement, which has misled those in power who have no way to provide benefits to the people. If we do not express our feelings and appeal to the country to exempt taxes and promote the national treasure, ink will cease to exist in the world. Now that the National Government is under political tutelage, the central committee members and ministers are all concerned about the people and are willing to listen to their needs. Therefore, we request that the council exert its efforts to assist in forwarding this request to the National Government, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, and the Ministry of Finance to approve the exemption of taxes on writing brushes and ink in accordance with the example of educational supplies, in order to promote education, reduce the burden of education, save the merchants who are on the verge of collapse, consolidate the foundation of the country, and preserve the national treasure. This is truly in the public interest. This is addressed to the Shanghai Special City Chamber of Commerce. The City Chamber of Commerce forwarded a document to the central government, stating that writing brushes and ink are related to educational supplies and requesting that they be exempted from tax in accordance with the example of books, in order to promote education. The situation is hereby forwarded for review and compliance. According to a letter from the Shanghai Writing Brush and Ink Trade Association dated the 10th of this month, "An investigation reveals that writing brushes and ink are educational supplies," and so on, regarding the preservation of national treasures, etc., the association investigated the raw materials for writing brushes and ink coming from distant provinces and foreign countries. They pay likin and consolidated taxes in the interior, and import and export taxes at customs. It is said that the total amount of taxes exceeds 20%. After the writing brushes and ink are manufactured, the customs tax paid for transporting them out of Shanghai is said to be more than 20% of the estimated value. Moreover, since 1927, labor costs have doubled, resulting in heavy capital and sluggish sales. It is estimated that the total sales at home and abroad are only about 500,000 yuan. The commercial situation is obviously difficult. It is believed that writing brushes and ink, in addition to being needed by public and private institutions and shops, are also sold to schools, which are ultimately educational supplies. The association stated that this tax revenue, calculated at 10% of the total annual sales, would amount to about 50,000 yuan, which is equivalent to only about 30,000 taels of customs silver. The total customs revenue of the Jianghai Customs is more than 20 million taels per year. This amount is only a drop in the bucket. In order to benefit students and alleviate the difficulties of merchants, the association requests that it be exempted from customs duties in accordance with the example of books. It seems that there is no obstacle to public expenditure. The situation is hereby forwarded to your government departments for review and approval, and that the order be forwarded for implementation. This is truly in the public interest. In addition to submitting this to the National Government, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, this is respectfully submitted to the National Government, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. On the 28th of this month, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce issued a reply stating that it had received the submission and had consulted the Ministry of Finance for review and handling. You are hereby notified accordingly.

Prohibition of Printing Superstitious Theories 145

The printing of superstitious matters in almanacs has always been prohibited. However, the almanacs for 1920 had already been compiled and printed by various bookstores, and the central government temporarily allowed them to remain in circulation out of consideration. Now that the almanacs for 1931 are being compiled, they should be strictly banned in order to promote good customs. Yesterday, the Bureau of Social Affairs specially instructed various book trade associations, stating that the theories of auspicious and inauspicious days, yin and yang, and the five elements are sufficient to promote superstition and obscure the people's wisdom. They must not be printed in the almanacs or calendars for 1931. Those who violate this order will be subject to confiscation and destruction, as well as penalties, as a warning to those who do not comply with the advice. The associations are hereby ordered to notify their members to comply. Furthermore, the Bureau's compilation of the almanacs for 1931 is nearing completion. If members of the associations need to print them, they may apply to the Bureau for verification and handling, etc. County Construction Bureau.

Progress on Abolishing the 2% Surtax 149

The French Concession Chinese Ratepayers Association convened an emergency meeting the day before yesterday to discuss ways to abolish the 2% surtax levied by the French Concession Municipal Council. The details of the meeting were reported in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday, the association cited the notice published by the French Concession Municipal Council on July 23, 1927, stating that "In order to avoid misunderstandings, the Municipal Council will levy a temporary special surtax of 2% in addition to the 12% property tax from July 1, 1927. The tax receipt will be printed with the words 'This receipt is for the collection of 12% property tax plus 2% temporary special surtax.' If the living standards and economic conditions gradually improve around January 1928, the Municipal Council may reconsider the property tax issue at that time," thereby confirming that the Municipal Council had already recognized that the 2% surtax was a temporary special surtax for six months and stated that the Municipal Council may reconsider the property tax issue around January 1928. However, the association found that the income of the French Municipal Council has increased year by year, and the income from property taxes alone has increased even more due to the increase in new construction and the imposition of additional charges based on the assessed value of the property. The abundance of its economic situation can be seen. Therefore, the association believes that the French Concession authorities have not considered the above notice for three years, which is regrettable. Furthermore, the Public Concession and the French Concession simultaneously increased the property tax by 2%. Now, the Public Concession has abolished the surtax, while the French Municipal Council has made no indication, which is even more unfair. In addition, the citizens are constantly questioning the association, making active negotiations imperative. It is also heard that a majority of citizens advocate that if the case cannot be resolved satisfactorily immediately, they should petition the new French Minister during the celebration of the French National Day.

Tian Tong Passed Away in Shanghai 152

Mr. Tian Tong, courtesy name Ziqin, was from Qichun, Hubei. He passed away at 1:00 PM on the 2nd of this month at the Shanghai Sino-Western Sanatorium. In 1905, Mr. Tian supported Dr. Sun Yat-sen in organizing the Tongmenghui in Tokyo, Japan, advocating the overthrow of the Qing Dynasty and the establishment of a republic. He was elected as a member of the Council and Director of the Secretariat. After the establishment of the Republic, he was elected as a member of the House of Representatives. After the failure of the Second Revolution, he fled to Tokyo, Japan. After Yuan Shikai's death, Mr. Tian returned and continued to serve as a member of the House of Representatives. Later, when Cao Kun planned to bribe his way to the presidency, Mr. Tian strongly advocated that the members of the House of Representatives move south, and Cao Kun ultimately failed. In 1926, when the revolutionary army arrived in Wuchang, Mr. Tian was appointed as the Jianghan Pacification Commissioner. After the South was pacified, he was ordered to be an envoy to Jin to persuade Yan Xishan to send troops to support the revolution and was elected as a member of the National Government. In 1928, he was appointed as a member of the Legislative Yuan but declined the position and retired to Shanghai to enjoy writing. He ran the Taiping Magazine, but suffered from overwork and contracted abdominal pain, which lasted for several months and ultimately led to his death. His coffin has now been moved to his residence at No. 72 Yongyu Lane, Belle Road, French Concession. In recent days, many people have come to pay their respects in plain cars and white horses.

Zhuang Songfu Establishes Donggang Shipping Company 154

Direct Sailings to Fenghua and Ninghai Now Available. Development of Ten Seaports in Eastern Zhejiang. Mr. Zhuang Songfu, former member of the Zhejiang Provincial Committee, has gathered funds to organize a large shipping company in order to facilitate commercial transport in Eastern Zhejiang and develop maritime transportation in Xiangshan, so as to benefit the people of Daishan, Xiangshan, Ninghai, and other places traveling to Shanghai and various ports. The preparations have been going on for many months and have now been successfully completed. The company officially opened today. The details of the company are as follows: Capital: The registered capital of the shipping company is 500,000 yuan, with the aim of developing a large port in the East, hence the company is named Donggang Shipping Company. The Shanghai head office is located opposite the water tower at the Damatou in the Nanshi. Branch offices are established in Xiangshan and Ninghai. The company's business is mainly transporting goods and passengers. Currently, one ship is operating first. Vessels: The company purchased a 1,000-ton steel ship for 80,000 yuan and named it Shengli. The entire ship has been overhauled and is brand new. Regular service is now being launched. The ship was originally scheduled to depart last night, but was delayed by one day due to the wind. The ship is docked at the Ning Shao No. 2 Wharf. The compradore is He Fengwen. If the business improves, passenger seats will be added to the ship. If it develops in the future, a second ship will be purchased. Routes: The ship is currently scheduled to travel from Shanghai to Daishan, Putuo, Shenjiamen, Guoyu, Dasong, Xiangshan, Fenghua, Ninghai, Xiashan, and Xueao. In the past, passengers and goods from these places had to transfer to civilian boats to Ningbo before transferring to ships to Shanghai. Now, they can sail directly, reducing the hardship of transshipment along the way. The schedule is tentatively set for Shanghai to depart on Mondays and Thursdays, and Ninghai to depart on Wednesdays and Saturdays.

Jiangsu and Zhejiang Silk Machinery Association.

Petition to Restrict the Establishment of New Cocoon Exchanges 156

The Jiangzhe Silk Weaving Joint Association previously resolved at an emergency general meeting to petition the government ministries and the Jiangzhe provincial governments to, based on the precedent of 1921, prohibit the establishment of new cocoon exchanges and cocoon stoves within the old prefectures of the two provinces. This was intended to enrich the raw materials for silk weaving and maintain the livelihood of industry and commerce. The drafting was done by the document section, revised and issued by the standing chairman Wang Jie’an. The telegram is recorded below (omitting titles). We believe that silk is an important industry with large production in our country. National tax revenue and the people's livelihood all depend on it. Since the mutual trade between China and foreign countries, various countries have competed to imitate and manufacture foreign silk fabrics, which are shipped to China for sale, increasing day by day. Because they lack raw silk materials, they come to China to compete for the purchase of fresh cocoons, absorbing them as much as possible. The general farmers also compete to sell cocoons for the convenience of sale. In the past, all were sold as silk, but now less than one in ten is sold this way. As a result, native silk is in great shortage and demand exceeds supply. There is a great difficulty in buying raw materials for silk weaving. This is the fundamental panic of the silk weaving industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. If a solution is not quickly sought, it is feared that the silk weaving industry, our important national essence, will disappear. In the spring of 1921, we drafted five articles for rectifying the silk industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces and submitted them to the Beijing Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce for review. On March 13 of the same year, the Ministry issued Order No. 500, revising them into six articles, ordering them to be followed. We received this order and found that the first article (No new cocoon exchanges or cocoon stoves shall be established in the old Hangzhou, Jiaxing, Huzhou, Shaoxing, and Zhuji prefectures of Zhejiang, and the old Ningbo, Suzhou, Changzhou, Zhenjiang, and Songjiang prefectures of Jiangsu, in order to enrich the raw materials for weaving) is a fundamental measure to protect the silk industry in the nine prefectures of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. However, over time, it was taken lightly and treated as a mere formality. In recent years, cocoon exchanges have sprung up like forests in the old prefectures, arbitrarily adding establishments without any restrictions. Among them, the Japanese merchants in Jiangsu are doing their best to purchase cocoons, which is especially ambitious, causing our country's silk weaving to have no silk to buy, forming a silk shortage. Therefore, the silk weaving industry in the two provinces has requested relief. Our association specially convened an emergency meeting of silk weaving colleagues from various places in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces on June 22 to discuss this case. The whole body unanimously resolved to petition the National Government, the Party Department, the ministries, and the governments and offices of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, requesting that the six articles of rectification measures be re-emphasized according to the precedent of 1921, and that a clear order be issued to maintain silk raw materials and enrich the national treasury's income, and to preserve raw materials, increase the production of domestic goods, and relieve unemployed workers. There is nothing better than this. It is reasonable to follow the discussion and submit the original method of justification, and to instruct the governments of the two provinces, cities, and counties to strictly restrict the establishment of new cocoon exchanges and cocoon stoves, and to pray for instructions to be followed. This is for the convenience of the Party. The Jiangsu and Zhejiang Silk Weaving Joint Association kowtows.

City General Labor Union Ends Under Orders 159

Preparatory Committee Issues Declaration The Shanghai Special City General Labor Union Preparatory Committee yesterday announced its conclusion under the instructions of the Municipal Party Department and issued the following declaration: The highest organ of the city's workers, the City General Labor Union Preparatory Committee, has today received instructions from the Municipal Party Department to end. On this last day, we have to say a few words to the workers. We have shouldered the mission of preparing the General Labor Union, and we have indeed worked hard for the preparatory work. This is proven by the facts. We hope that the formal General Labor Union will be established within three months, so as not to disappoint the commission of the Municipal Party Department and the expectations of the workers. At the same time, we are also workers, and of course we also hope that the General Labor Union can be established as soon as possible. The date of the establishment of the association was September last year, when the Labor Union Law had not yet been promulgated, so in our ideal, the formal General Labor Union must be a matter of course. Unexpectedly, in November last year, the Labor Union Law that workers had been looking forward to was promulgated, but in this Labor Union Law, there is no General Labor Union. Then the General Labor Union lost the legal basis, and the future of the association was also thorny. Three months after the establishment of the association, all the preparatory work was completed. We represented the will of the city's workers and submitted a request to the superior level for approval to establish a formal General Labor Union. However, the Municipal Party Department could not accommodate our request because of the Labor Union Law. We submitted more than a dozen documents requesting the establishment of the General Labor Union. At the same time, members of the Municipal Party Department once petitioned the central government for the General Labor Union issue. However, the central government has consistently refused to allow it because of the law. A few days ago, the Municipal Party Department received instructions from the central government to revoke the association. Therefore, the Municipal Party Department formally instructed the association yesterday to end the day and send personnel to organize the industry labor union associations, such as the publishing industry, yarn factory industry, etc., to share the association. In this environment, there is indeed no better way to establish the General Labor Union. We can only follow the instructions of the Party Department and completely end it today, and wait for the personnel to take over. This is the process of the association's end that workers should know. The General Labor Union Committee ends today. As long as the workers can realize that they are moving towards the right path of developing production and relieving the suffering of workers, and redoubling their efforts, the labor movement will also have a bright day. We hope that the workers will continue to hold the revolutionary spirit of the workers and continue to work hard and forge ahead. This is what we are praying for today. News of the Development of Anti-Drug Association Affairs 161

The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association has recently been expanding its affairs, and in addition to assigning commissioners to handle the work of each department on a daily basis, it has also formed ten subcommittees. In the event of special accidents and development plans, the subcommittees are responsible for properly arranging coping methods and sending them to the Standing Committee for discussion. The committee includes ten subcommittees: attendance, economy, patrol and transportation, branches, propaganda, library, publishing, promotion, communication, and competition. Each group holds a meeting once a week and a joint meeting of each group once every two weeks to report on the progress of each group. The association has more than 400 anti-drug comrade associations in various places, and the scope is the widest. It is difficult to manage, and many of them have not been able to follow the association's regulations and plans due to lack of economic talent. The association has specially reduced the scope and uniformly changed to anti-drug propaganda associations, which are responsible for awakening compatriots and publicizing anti-drug efforts, and must not hear about other matters. Detailed regulations are currently being drafted by the subcommittee and will be announced to the branches in various places soon. Its nature is different from that of the Anti-Drug Comrades Association. Those that have already been established, the association also intends to re-strictly stipulate and send personnel to visit the branches in various places. The association also intends to send personnel to organize those that have not been established in order to strengthen support. Recently, overseas Chinese have successively reported on the establishment of branches, and foreign sympathetic groups have recently sent personnel to the association for contact, such as the German Women's Grand Alliance and the British Women's Suffrage Association, etc., have sent representatives to China to express cooperation with the association, and Director General Huang has received them separately, and stated the determination of our people to reject drugs, hoping for international cooperation. The League of Nations' Special Committee on Narcotic Drugs will hold a meeting at the end of this year to discuss the issue of narcotic drugs. China has suffered greatly from narcotic drugs, and the relationship with this meeting is extremely important. The association is currently preparing materials and intends to send personnel to report on the state of China's drug abuse and expose the great powers' conspiracy to poison China. The association hopes that all sectors will pay attention to this. Health Bureau

News of the Preparation of the Anti-Smuggling Training Institute 167

The Anti-Smuggling Department of the Ministry of Finance established a training institute to cultivate cadres and talents for the anti-smuggling team. The institute was established in accordance with the army establishment. Huang Qiguang was appointed as the Major General Director and Zhang Yuannan as the Colonel Dean of Education. The preparatory office of the training institute was established on June 15 and rented No. 19 Wenmiao Road, Laoximen as the site. There are a total of 65 internal officers and staff members, most of whom were appointed by the Ministry of Finance and the Anti-Smuggling Department separately and arrived at the post successively. The military officer team recruited 160 students, who were directly consulted by the Anti-Smuggling Department to send to various agencies for examination. Those who graduated from junior high school or have served as lieutenants are qualified. The examination will be held on the 15th of this month, and the class will officially start on August 1. 680 soldiers will be selected by the Anti-Smuggling Headquarters under the Anti-Smuggling Department, the first and second special regiments, and those who are under the age of 25 and have both academic and excellent character and strong physique will be selected to serve. The graduation period is set for six months, and the treatment is generous. The treatment for the students and soldiers is the same as that of the police training team of the Nanjing Army, Navy and Air Force Headquarters. Director Huang of the institute convened a first institute affairs meeting yesterday to discuss the institute's affairs.

The Observatory Reported the Rainfall of the Day Before Yesterday 168

Totaling 3.27 Inches The heavy rain the day before yesterday was rare in peacetime. According to the Xujiahui Observatory, it rained a total of 3.27 inches in one day. According to the records, from January 1 to the present, it has rained 25.85 inches, which is about 3 inches more than the average rainfall of 22.92 inches during the same period in the past 56 years. French Concession

Also Prohibits Reckless Honking of Car Horns 169

The Da Wan Bao said that in order to reduce the noise in the city, the French Concession Public Works Bureau has recently ordered that drivers of cars in the concession should not honk their horns unless it is absolutely necessary. Whenever it is necessary to honk the horn, a rubber horn should be used first and the sound should not be prolonged. Especially from 11 pm to 6 am, silence should be maintained as much as possible. If there are obstacles in front, the speed should be reduced and the horn should not be honked lightly to urge people in the house to pay attention. All indiscriminate honking of horns is strictly prohibited.

New Red Flashing Light Installed in Zhangjiabang 170

To Be Turned on Around the 21st The Navigation Department of the Customs Service announced that the office has checked the new lights installed in the Huangpu River within the concession by the Jianghai Customs Tax Department and listed the situation and trend on the left. Shanghai Huangpu River is now planning to install a small-sized non-listed red flashing light. The light will be turned on around July 21. When the time comes, it will be implemented without further notice. The light is set on a steel lighthouse 15 feet high on the south bank of the Zhangjiabang waterway, Section C of the Shanggang, that is, the Yitaixing Coal Yard. The light will flash once every three seconds, that is, it will be bright for three tenths of a second and go out for two and seven tenths of a second. All nautical charts Nos. 1 and 9 printed by the Maritime Administration should be corrected accordingly. Therefore, it should be followed and announced that all ships must be careful and remember to avoid negligence. This is announced on June 30, 1930.

News from Various Trade Associations 174

Biscuit, Candy and Canned Food Industry The Shanghai Biscuit, Candy and Canned Food Industry Association, in view of the fact that the price of various raw materials is affected by the price of gold and has soared by multiples, but it is still sold at the old price, which is difficult to maintain the cost. A meeting was convened yesterday. Zhang Yibiao, the chairman, reported the purpose of the meeting and said that although many of the raw materials used in the industry are domestic, such as sugar, spices, colors, tin cans, iron sheets, printing paper, etc., either directly or indirectly, most of them depend on foreign goods, and the import price has soared. The only way to remedy this is to appropriately increase the selling price for capital injection. As a result of the discussion, it was publicly decided that the price of thick and thin biscuits, whether in bulk or canned, should be temporarily increased by 10%. The price of canned meat, vegetables and fruits should be increased by 2 to 4 points per can, and the price of various candies should also be temporarily increased by 10%. In addition, in the case of the labor dispute between Tailai and labor, it was publicly decided to grant two months of retirement pay, which was certified by the association and signed by both parties. In the case of the Chinese-owned capital dispute, it was publicly decided to write a letter to persuade the shareholders to abandon their prejudices and take care of the overall situation. The case of eliminating wild chickens running on the street and selling unsealed canned biscuits, which is harmful to hygiene and the reputation of the industry, was publicly decided to present to the Health and Social Bureaus to jointly and effectively eliminate it. Page 15

Local News Two

A Withered Beauty 176

A Visit with Huang Baiying 177

Baiying's Outraged Words Against Sanmao

Said That Woman Will Surely Be Punished by Law

Will Testify and Describe Everything at Next Hearing

The case of the dancer Huang Baiying being forced to take poison has caused a great uproar in Shanghai. Since the incident, the newspapers have raced to publish detailed reports, though with some discrepancies. However, the main points are as reported in this newspaper a day earlier. Since Baiying suffered this misfortune, she has been staying indoors. The singing and dancing venues are all talking about this. As the facts of this case have already been presented to the readers, and Bai Niang, a weak woman, was fiercely loved by Zhang and Tong, and the ending has taken a strange turn, the matter is similar to Haggard's novels. The remnants of flowers and drifting catkins are filled with sadness, and her situation is also pitiful. Therefore, I took some time one evening to visit Bai and have a heart-to-heart red-light night talk, which only increased my feelings of being a rootless duckweed. I will describe it in detail below.

Baiying Yesterday 178

Photo by this newspaper's reporter

Baiying Writes Another Heartbreaking Letter 179

My heart is broken as I write this letter. You can only read the words and perhaps imagine the situation at the time. Under the lamp, I quietly watched her supporting the table and writing. The pen moved rapidly, and her resentment flowed from her wrist. Baiying's face showed fear and determination. After finishing each sentence, she would bite her lip and nod, her fingers trembling slightly, and her loose hair hanging down. She would often brush it up with her left hand. After finishing, she handed it to me to read. The words read: "Hui Lin, I did not expect your graduation ceremony to trigger my death. But when you know I am dead, do not be sad. People are all going to die anyway. But I only worry about Aunt Yi and my sister. They are my confidantes and understand me the most. Although this death is forced upon me, it can also show my love for you, Baiying." After reading, I glanced at Baiying and said, "Doesn't this language of yours indicate a determination long ago? The descriptions are so sad." Bai raised her voice and said, "I would rather sacrifice myself. Mr. Zhang's parents are both alive and he already has a wife. I definitely don't want to implicate others because of me." The heartbreaking note and the last words faced each other, making one feel sad.

The Guest Room is Elegantly Furnished 180

Baiying's residence is in the French Concession, in the Wanyi Lane on Luban Road. The house is very new and she has only moved in recently. I sent in my card, and an old woman answered the door. "Does the gentleman want to meet Miss? Please sit down for a moment while I go upstairs to inform her." So I sat down on the sofa and looked around. The furnishings in the room were quite simple. In the center was a small rectangular table, covered with a rose-colored felt tablecloth. On the table was a flower basket. From a distance, the buds seemed to have all bloomed and lacked vitality. But upon closer inspection, they were paper-made wax flowers. A long sofa was placed against the wall, with two chairs on either side. In the corner of the room were a refrigerator and a gramophone, and another cabinet with various glassware. Near the window, long curtains hung down to the ground, and one could roughly see the inside of the room from the door. On the wall hung a small portrait of Baiying and three or four photos of movie stars. Under the ceiling, a large gauze lamp hung, and the light was soft. I waited for about two or three minutes, and then the once-famous Bai Niang gracefully entered the room.

Her Appearance is Extremely Haggard 181

I first heard a slight cough coming from the inner room. Looking back, it was indeed Baiying. Her curly hair was draped over her shoulders, almost covering her eyebrows, and her appearance was extremely haggard. Under the lamp, she looked even paler. She bowed slightly as she greeted me, and I saw that her feet were bare, wearing only slippers made of white satin covered with red flowers. After exchanging pleasantries, I asked, "The court hearing was held a few days ago, but you didn't go. I suppose it was because you weren't feeling well?" Bai replied, "Indeed, as you say. The doctor ordered me to rest and not to talk. And since being forced to take the poison, I have been confused and haven't recovered all day. I'm afraid that my illness would affect my testimony." That evening, Bai Niang wore a short-sleeved top and a vest of apricot green, while the vest was white with black edges. The color of her pants was the same as her top.

Baiying's Nervousness 182

"Did the lady also provide any information about Mr. Tong?" Baiying hesitated slightly, then spoke frankly, "If the judge asks me how Mr. Tong should be punished, I will only follow the court's decision. That woman will surely be punished by law, no need to say more." At this time, Bai had already sat down, facing inward with both hands on the table. Whenever she spoke of the words "Mr. Tong," she would frown and show displeasure. I asked about the already revealed facts, such as going out from the dance hall, driving around in the western suburbs of Shanghai, and taking poison in the hotel. She either nodded in agreement or tapped the table to indicate corrections. Her expression was very nervous.

Her Upper Eyelids Were Slightly Red and Purple 183

Baiying's pale face, reflected by the lamp, revealed a look of fatigue. Her eyelashes were often closed, and her upper eyelids were slightly red and purple. One could imagine the severity of her illness. Everything she said was very moving. She claimed that after taking the medicine, she forced herself to stay awake, walking back and forth in the room and circling it several times. Tong forced her to sit down, but she refused each time. After being forced repeatedly, she sat on the sofa, and Tong put his arms on the back of the chair, his face sinking as he said to Bai, "What exactly do you want?" Meaning, to marry or to die. Bai resolutely replied, "Nothing." This was a firm rejection. Bai often used English phrases when talking to me, such as "Marry or die" and "I don't care."

Will Testify and Describe Everything at the Hearing 184

I asked again, "Will the lady also prepare to appear in court next Monday when the court hearing is held?" Bai replied, "At that time, I will testify and describe everything in detail to clarify the truth and seek the judgment of the law." Bai was very excited during her speech. Judging from her behavior and listening to her conversation, I think she is neurotic. Fearing that too much talk would harm her health, I immediately took my leave.

A Big Fire in Nanshi Last Night 185

Yiyuan Medicinal Material Store Was Careless

Total Losses Amounted to Over 20,000 Gold

The Yiyuan Medicinal Material Store, No. 26 Xunjidao in Nanshi, suddenly caught fire at around 7:00 PM last night. All the stored medicinal materials were reduced to ashes, with losses of over 10,000 gold. It was found that the Yiyuan Medicinal Material Store has been operating in Guo Xian Gua Street for many years, with a large scale. The shop owner and manager is Jiang Jixiang, and the assistant manager is Zhu Baohua. Their warehouse has six buildings and several bungalows, guarded by the old accountant Gao Ruqi. He goes to the shop during the day and sleeps in the warehouse at night. At around 7:00 PM last night, Mr. Gao had not yet returned to the warehouse. During this time, the clerk of the engraving shop next door suddenly saw green smoke rising from the warehouse. Knowing that there was a fire, he immediately sent an apprentice to the pharmacy to ask Gao to return. When Gao arrived, the fire was raging and there was no way to put it out. The fire department rushed to the scene after receiving the alarm and tried their best to put out the fire. It was not until 8:30 PM that it gradually subsided. All six buildings were burned down, and the stored medicinal materials were also reduced to ashes. The medicinal materials were worth about 15,000 yuan, plus the buildings, totaling no less than 20,000 gold. The cause of the fire may have been caused by throwing cigarette butts. It is still under investigation. Fortunately, the surrounding neighbors were not affected; otherwise, the losses would have been even greater. Coastal Ships

Were Again Stopped by Wind Yesterday 186

Datong Wheel Damaged its Propeller and Stopped Sailing

The other day, Shanghai experienced a strong wind, and the Tai Gu Ning Shao's Shanghai-Ningbo rounds were all suspended, and the commercial rounds along the Zhejiang coast were also blocked for a day. Yesterday afternoon, there was a hurricane warning, and various commercial rounds in Shanghai were again blocked and could not exit. The situation is described below.

First Wind Blockade

The first strong wind occurred on the 2nd. In addition to the formal announcement of the suspension of the Xin Beijing and Xin Ning Shao rounds, the Shanghai-Taiwan rounds, Wenzhou rounds, and Chuanshan rounds of Zhejiang Shipping also did not dare to set sail. Only the Yangtze River round operated as usual. It was not until noon yesterday that the wind gradually subsided, and the blocked Wen, Tai, and Zhoushan rounds were able to exit one after another. There were more than a dozen rounds entering Wusong yesterday noon to avoid the wind. In total, 29 ships came to Shanghai yesterday, most of which were delayed due to the wind blockade.

Second Suspension

Yesterday, the Shanghai-Ningbo rounds of China Merchants' Xin Jiangtian and Sanbei's Ningxing rounds had loaded all the export goods and passengers at around 3:00 PM and were waiting to depart at 5:00 PM. However, at around 5:00 PM, the Jianghai Customs issued a notice stating that according to the observatory report, there would be strong winds on the sea that night, making navigation very dangerous. Please stop the exit of the two rounds. After receiving the report, China Merchants Sanbei stated that the two rounds to Putuo were mostly booked by passengers. If they were suspended this time, the losses would be huge. They sent someone to the Customs to inquire about whether they could still depart. As a result, they were afraid of danger. For the safety of passengers, the two bureaus decided to suspend the voyage with pain. At around 6:00 PM, they notified the passengers, stating that the suspension due to wind avoidance was due to the Customs' intention and could not be forced. At this time, many passengers left the ship and went ashore.

Blocked Ships

After the customs warning was issued, more than a dozen coastal rounds that were scheduled to depart yesterday, such as Shengli, etc., were unable to depart. The docks in Nanshi were almost full, all waiting for orders to start. Most of them will have to wait until today to depart.

Datong Engine Damage

The Tai Gu Company's Yangtze River round Datong was scheduled to depart on Thursday yesterday. This time, the round came to Shanghai from Hankou downstream. While traveling, the rudder blade of its engine suddenly broke and could not operate. After the ship arrived in Shanghai, it unloaded all the cargo and towed it into the shipyard for major repairs. It will have to stop for ten days, resulting in the company's Yangtze River rounds being empty yesterday and no ship departing. Qin Liang Fights with Anger Over

Wife Smokes Opium, Daughter Prostitutes

Unable to Stop, Unwilling to Live

Qin Liangfa, a 53-year-old man from Ningbo, boarded the Ketai ferry at the Hankou Road dock at around 10:00 AM the day before yesterday to cross the Huangpu River. When the round arrived at the Puxi surface of Lujiazui, Qin suddenly took advantage of the unpreparedness and jumped into the river to commit suicide. Fortunately, the sailor rescued him on the spot and sent him to the Water Patrol Police Station. According to his confession, he lived at No. 34 Sanxin Lane, Ainage Road, Beizhu Bridge, French Concession, and was originally a foreign goods broker. His parents, both over 70 years old, were still in his hometown. He was the second of three brothers. His wife, Zhu, was from Jiangbei, 39 years old, and had two sons and a daughter. The eldest son, who was twenty, was learning the foreign goods business. The second son, who was twelve, was sent to a voluntary school by his wife. The daughter, named Yongdi, was sixteen. At the age of fourteen, she was pawned by his wife to Han Village in the same village (commonly known as Salted Meat Village) for prostitution, with a limit of six months and a pawn price of 140 yuan. In June last year, she was redeemed at the original price. However, his wife was addicted to opium and still relied on her daughter to sell her body to make a living. Seeing his wife and daughter taking this low path, he repeatedly tried to stop them, but they would not listen. Therefore, he was angry and threw himself into the river to end everything. It was the truth. The police station sent detective Huang Songsheng to go to the address and summon his wife, Zhu, and daughter, Yongdi, to the police station. According to Zhu's confession, the family was extremely poor, and her husband had no major income. She had no choice but to let her daughter engage in this lowly profession to make a living. Yongdi also confessed that after being redeemed last year, she met a patron who loved her very much. He voluntarily wanted to marry her, but seeing her father's violent temper, the agreement was terminated. Her father's obstruction caused the relationship to break down, and she was unable to escape the lowly profession. It was the thing she hated the most in her life. After verifying the confession, the police chief ordered the detective to transfer the three to the local court in the afternoon. Prosecutor Yang specially opened the court (the court was originally scheduled to stop hearing in the afternoon during the summer vacation) and conducted a preliminary hearing. According to the previous confessions of the three, the judge announced his opinion and first sent Qin's wife, Zhu, to the hospital to quit smoking. Qin nodded in agreement. The official asked Yongdi who she wanted to follow, and she replied that she wanted to follow her mother. The official said that if she followed her mother, she would also have to be sent to the hospital. When Yongdi heard this, she was unwilling. The judge ruled in court that Yongdi should be returned to her father for custody. Zhu was returned to the hospital. Unexpectedly, as soon as the father and daughter left the court, Yongdi suddenly shouted for a rickshaw, sat in it alone, and left, ignoring Qin. Qin tried to stop her, but it was too late. He watched Yongdi disappear from near to far. Qin only shouted in anger and returned home in frustration.

A Fierce Battle of Detectives and Thieves 189

Robbed Fifty Yuan

Two Thieves Arrested

At around 8:00 PM yesterday, three thieves stood in front of the Shengtai South Goods Store at No. 1057 Linping Road, Yangshupu, Shanghai East, but did not rob because there were still several people buying food in the store at that time. The thieves did not move. After a while, the buyers dispersed, and the three thieves entered the store and searched the counter. However, the Shengtai South Goods Store was located in a remote area of Shanghai East, and the business was not very prosperous. The daily income was limited. As a result, they robbed 50 yuan. After the thieves left the store, the shop assistants rushed to report to the nearby police. The Chinese police, outnumbered, immediately reported to the Yangshupu Police Station by telephone. The police chief rushed the Chinese and foreign detectives in a police car to the destination to chase the thieves. The car was very fast, and in a flash, it had passed the destination. Seeing three people walking on the road, their expressions were panicked and they were walking fast. The detectives knew they were not good people and shouted for them to stop. The three ran wildly again. The detectives immediately got out of the car, and the three pulled out their guns and aimed at the detectives. Because of poor eyesight, they did not hit. The detectives, for self-defense, immediately drew their guns and returned fire. For a time, bullets rained down, and pedestrians took cover. As a result, two of the three thieves were injured and fell to the ground. One thief ran away. A gun was found beside the thieves. The detectives immediately sent the two thieves to the Bureau of Works hospital for treatment and further interrogation.

Autopsy on a Couple Who Died Tragically from Electrocution 196

How Should Electrical Appliances Be Installed? Careful Inspection Is Necessary to Avoid Future Troubles. At 11:00 AM the day before yesterday, during a sudden rainstorm, Chen, the wife of Liu Zhaolian, the owner of a sesame cake stall at the corner of Haifang Road and Gordon Road in West Shanghai, leaned against the counter of the cigarette and paper shop at No. 709 next door, holding onto the iron railing on the counter. Because the iron railing was in contact with an electrical wire, the iron conducted electricity, and the current flowed into her body. She immediately became numb and fell to the ground. Her husband, upon hearing the news, rushed over to help her up. As soon as he touched her, the electricity in her body was transmitted to Liu Zhaolian, and he also fell to the ground. The Gordon Road police precinct was notified and dispatched detectives to the scene, who managed to transport the couple to Dehe Hospital for treatment. However, the electrical poisoning spread rapidly, and by the time they arrived at the hospital, the poison had already reached their hearts, and they both died. The two bodies were then transported to the Feilun Road morgue for an autopsy. Detectives were ordered to investigate whether the electrical appliances in the shop were installed according to the regulations of the Public Works Department. If the installation was improper, they were ordered to correct it to prevent future troubles. Yesterday morning, the Special District Local Court was requested to send Prosecutor Xu to the morgue for an autopsy. It was confirmed that they had died from electric shock. However, according to the Western constable, the installation of the electrical appliances and the cause of the accident had not yet been determined and required further investigation. Prosecutor Xu, noting that the couple had no relatives in Shanghai, ordered their bodies to be handed over to the Pushan Villa for coffining and burial. The police were ordered to investigate and verify whether there was any negligence in the installation of the electric meter in the cigarette and paper shop.

Further Interrogation in the Wang Baosan Murder Case 198

All the Accused Recanted Their Previous Confessions, Awaiting Interrogation of Witnesses. Wang Baosan, who ran a night soil business at the Xiangyan Bridge on Hu's Family Wooden Bridge, was murdered due to jealousy and competition for business with Dai Ruzhao and others in the same trade. On the evening of the first day of the second month of the lunar calendar this year, Dai Zhizhao colluded with Shi Fulin, Zhu Zixiang, Liu Luguanzi, Wang Guangfu, and others to go to Wang Baosan's house and shoot him to death. The Public Security Bureau arrested Dai, Shi, Zhu, Liu, and others and transferred them to the Local Court. Dai and the others had already been sentenced to life imprisonment and imprisonment for ten years or more. Now, the accomplices in the same case, Wang Guangfu and Wang Wankui, were also arrested by the Municipal Public Security Bureau. After interrogation, they confessed to participating in the conspiracy and committing the murder. They were sent to the Local Court and also prosecuted. Yesterday morning, Magistrate Qian held a court session to interrogate the accused. Wang Guangfu and Wang Wankui both claimed that they did not participate in the murder of Wang Baosan. They stated that the confessions to the Public Security Bureau were completely fabricated and that they were forced to admit it after being subjected to private torture, including hanging. The judge then summoned the widow, Wang Shi, to testify. Wang Shi testified that Wang Baosan was her husband and that Liu Luguanzi, Wang Fuguang, and Dai Ruzhao killed her husband. It was on the first day of the second lunar month. Shi Fulin first came to her house and said that a boat had arrived and needed to be loaded with night soil. After Shi Fulin finished speaking and left, she went to close the door, and Liu Luguanzi immediately pushed the door open and shot her husband. Liu Luguanzi fired a total of four shots, hitting her husband's left hand, leg, back, and left rib. At that time, Zhu Zixiang also said that the person was not dead, so Dai Ruzhao fired another shot. She was near the table at the time, so Dai Ruzhao grabbed her and threw her aside, and Wang Guangfu kicked her away, and they fled. Wang Wankui was acting as a lookout outside the door. Shi Jinlin testified that Wang Baosan was her brother-in-law. She did not see him die. She heard her sister shouting for help at home. She was a neighbor and opened the door to see Wang Guangfu, Liu Luguanzi, Dai Ruzhao, Zhu Zixiang, Wang Wankui, Shi Fulin, and six or seven other people running away. At this point, the judge questioned Wang Wankui, who claimed that he had gone to Chongming with Zhang Youlang on the twenty-ninth day of the first month and returned home on the ninth day of the second month. Zhang Youlang lived in Qiyaozhen in Chongming. Wang Guangfu claimed that if Wang Shi had grabbed Dai Ruzhao and said that he kicked her away, why didn't he shoot her since he had a pistol at the time, leaving no evidence of his crime? At this point, the judge considered it necessary to have further evidence in the case and adjourned the hearing to a later date. The accused were returned to custody.

It dissolves more easily than other milk powders and coarse milk substitutes, leaving no residue and with minimal waste. The rally was particularly interesting due to special circumstances, making it more interesting than other rallies. The rally route was 600 miles long, starting from Gothenburg on the west coast, passing through the forests and mountains of central Sweden, north to Gävle on the east coast, and then along the coast to Stockholm. In addition to muddy roads, the route included slippery and windy streets with deep snow. Sometimes the cars were buried in snow, and the nighttime temperature was below zero degrees Celsius. Cars in the A-level rally should normally maintain an average speed of 34 to 37 miles per hour, but due to driving conditions on narrow, snowy, and winding roads, they had to travel at 50 miles per hour. There were stations along the way to manage the rally. Each car was limited to a 15-minute stop at each station. In addition, they could stop for half an hour after traveling half the distance. If the driver could race the entire route within an "ideal range," their name would be engraved on the "Winter Silver Cup." Those who achieve three victories would be awarded the trophy. The Lincoln Motor Company proclaims that the car manufacturing report published by the company states that each important part of the Lincoln car has been inspected separately. The company employs chemists, metallurgists, and scientists to conduct inspections and is equipped with various sophisticated instruments for this purpose. If any parts or materials do not meet the specified highest standards, they will be rejected upon arrival. All steel used for forging must have its appearance inspected by the company's chemical laboratory before shipment. It must be inspected again during shipment. Each time, it cannot be shipped without the approval of the chemical laboratory. Forged parts must also be inspected for the composition of their original material, as their hardness, strength, and various flaws cannot be distinguished by visual inspection. If it is found to be inconsistent with the specified standards, it will not be made into machine parts. Cast parts must be thoroughly inspected to ensure their stability. For example, each crankcase is hammered and drilled to ensure that there is no air inside. The various parts inside the Lincoln car, such as carburetors, generators, distributors, vacuum boxes, and speedometers, are purchased from companies specializing in manufacturing these parts. Each part is inspected when it arrives at the factory, not only inspecting the appearance of the entire batch of parts. This so-called thorough inspection is designed to supplement the Lincon factory representative stationed at the company supplying the parts. Book and Newspaper Reviews

Rudiments of Philosophy by Wu Yuyang 207

Written by A.S. Rappoport, Translated by Chen Xunshao, Published by The Commercial Press.

Philosophy is a discipline that studies the principles of various phenomena and their overall relationships. I believe that anyone who studies any discipline or handles affairs in society should study philosophy and understand philosophy. This is because I always feel that those who study specialized disciplines and those who handle affairs in society, because they do not understand philosophy, only go around in circles within their own specialized disciplines when studying, and only know how to treat the head when it hurts and the foot when it hurts in society, unable to see the fundamental causes of various phenomena and unable to find an overall solution. This is not nonsense; if you pay close attention to others and yourself, you will understand. I originally studied political science, but I started my studies with philosophy. This is a matter of experience.

However, among all disciplines, perhaps none is as easily misunderstood by the general public as philosophy. The general public always thinks that philosophy is a kind of ethereal and unsubstantial thing, and studying philosophy is an idle pursuit. It is true that it is difficult to find a suitable philosophy book, especially introductory books, published in China in the past. They all explain philosophy too mystically, almost making readers unable to grasp the main point. Often, many enthusiastic young men and women give up reading philosophy books halfway through. And the teachers who teach philosophy courses in the first year of university often just copy and paste from various sources, using a large number of terms as magic weapons to show off their skills, making students dizzy. Universities also do not pay attention to this discipline at all (the opposite of European universities), so by the time they graduate from university, they are still confused. The problem of not understanding philosophy mentioned earlier is unavoidable. The above remarks are only to illustrate the importance of philosophy and attract attention. As for how to understand philosophy and arouse interest in research, I would like to recommend a book that may be of some help to everyone.

This book, "Rudiments of Philosophy," was recently published by The Commercial Press. I do not know the author or translator at all, but because I have read it carefully, I recognize its inherent value, so I dare to recommend it to everyone. Now, let me first introduce the contents of this book, and then introduce its advantages.

This book is divided into three parts. The first part is the meaning and content of philosophy, the second part is the evolution and trends of philosophy, and the third part is the schools and important issues of philosophy. These three parts can be said to explain the entire scope of philosophy to us.

The first part is introductory in nature, breaking open the mystery of philosophy for us. This part is divided into eight chapters. The first chapter is an introduction, explaining that the main idea of philosophy is to "explain the essence, origin, and interrelationships of all things." This definition could not be more comprehensive. It also explains that philosophy is divided into three major categories for the convenience of research: (1) singular problems (pure philosophy), (2) plural problems (natural philosophy), and (3) individual problems of living things (philosophy of life). Finally, it introduces the contents of philosophy: (1) metaphysics, (2) psychology, (3) epistemology, (4) logic, (5) aesthetics, (6) ethics, (7) philosophy of law, and (8) sociology and philosophy of history. The subsequent chapters provide an overview of each of the contents mentioned above.

The second part is a historical narrative, allowing us to understand the origins and trends of Western philosophy. This part is divided into five chapters. The first chapter is an introduction, explaining the periodization of the history of philosophy: (1) ancient period, (2) Middle Ages, (3) modern period, and (4) recent period. The subsequent four chapters provide an overview of these four periods, highlighting their important points and providing insightful critiques. In the fourth chapter, "Modern Period," the characteristics of the national character of various European countries are presented as the reason for the creation of various modern philosophical thoughts, with a critical eye.

The third part explains the schools of philosophy and their issues. This part is divided into five chapters. The first chapter states that the three ends of philosophy to be solved are: (1) content, (2) method, and (3) cause. For the convenience of research, the problems of philosophy are summarized into three major categories: (1) problems of pure philosophy, (2) problems of moral philosophy, and (3) problems of intellectual philosophy. The second chapter discusses the problems of pure philosophy, introducing the three major schools of modern pure philosophers concerning the basics of the existence of the universe: idealism, materialism, and dualism of mind and matter, and clarifies their origins. The third chapter discusses the problems of moral philosophy, presenting the moral problems that philosophers of all ages have pondered to solve: (1) the origin of moral concepts, (2) the obedience to moral concepts.

The fourth chapter discusses intellectual philosophy, dividing the content and function of intellectual philosophy into three items for explanation, which are: (1) The origin of Zhi, (2) Where Zhi comes from or its original problem, (3) Can Zhi be sought or its effectiveness and scope problem. The last chapter of the conclusion puts forward two problems to be solved by philosophy, the first is that philosophy should strive to solve, namely, what is the existant, how can things exist, what do we know, what is our duty, why are we so inferior. The second is that philosophy has a close relationship with the things of everyday existence, philosophy cannot be separated from reality, so the problem of philosophy is endless.

We can see the advantages of this book from its content, that is, it can systematically explain the whole field of philosophy in a small booklet, giving us a very clear concept of the outline of philosophy, the history of philosophical thought, and the important problems of philosophy. And its method of explanation is also very clear, and it can be added to a more objective criticism, so that beginners will not be confused about the system of philosophy and have the danger of preconceptions. As for the fluency of the translation and the popularity of the translation names, I also feel when I read it.

Finally, I have something to say, I introduce this introductory and small philosophy book, maybe some people say I am too boring, in fact, I do not know how to introduce profound and magnificent books, but the introductory is not clear what the profound can be said of, not from the smaller start, what is the meaning of grand works, I think the general public in society needs a kind of philosophical cultivation of riding a horse to give them a little guidance to study and work, as long as you spend a little time you can finish reading it, and it is also very worthwhile when life is busy and the heat is difficult to bear.

Manuscript Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Reviews 209

(1) The text is limited to introducing the latest publications at home and abroad. In addition to literary works, all political, economic, legal, scientific, educational, etc., books and newspapers are included in the introduction, but frivolous books will not be introduced.

(2) Articles on textual research or research on ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(3) Pictures and photographs are limited to those related to the text.

(4) Each article should not exceed 3,000 characters.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write manuscripts horizontally, and do not write illegibly. Western text should be omitted where possible. If it is necessary to cite the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink to draw pictures in the manuscript, and do not use colored paper. Use white paper and black drawings.

(8) Please indicate that the manuscript is to be sent to the Book and Newspaper Review Department.

(9) Manuscripts will not be returned whether or not they are published. If a return is required, it should be stated in advance and sufficient postage should be attached.

(10) Remuneration for texts is divided into three types: four yuan, three yuan, and two yuan per thousand characters. The same applies to each picture and photograph. Remuneration for special manuscripts will be calculated separately. Wu Ben Girl Xiao Yao Zhaoying plays Princess Youxi, Bing photo.
